# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Produce answer.json** — Write ALL output to `/workspace/answer.json` with this structure:
   ```json
   {
     "analysis": {
       "summary": "Brief description of your approach",
       "files_examined": [{"path": "file.ext", "description": "..."}],
       "reasoning": "Detailed explanation or analysis"
     },
     "changes": [
       {"file": "path.ext", "description": "...", "diff": "unified diff"}
     ]
   }
   ```
   Omit `changes` if the task is analysis-only. Do NOT edit source files directly — produce diffs in `changes[]` instead.

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

---

# big-code-quantlib-arch-001: QuantLib Barrier Option Pricing Chain

## Task

Trace the QuantLib pricing chain for a barrier option: instrument→pricing engine→term structure→stochastic process→path generator. Map how a call to BarrierOption.NPV() propagates through the Instrument/LazyObject calculate() mechanism, into the pricing engine (analytic or Monte Carlo), through the term structure queries, stochastic process evolution, and path generation.

## Context

- **Repository**: lballabio/QuantLib (C++, ~450K LOC)
- **Category**: Architectural Understanding
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: ql/instruments/, ql/pricingengines/barrier/, ql/processes/, ql/termstructures/, ql/methods/montecarlo/

## Requirements

1. Identify all relevant components in the pricing chain from BarrierOption through to PathGenerator
2. Trace the dependency chain from NPV() through LazyObject.calculate() → Instrument.performCalculations() → engine.calculate()
3. Document how the McSimulation framework connects MonteCarloModel, PathGenerator, and PathPricer
4. Explain the term structure hierarchy (YieldTermStructure, BlackVolTermStructure) and how the stochastic process (GeneralizedBlackScholesProcess) uses them

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — role in architecture
- path/to/file2.ext — role in architecture
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Entry point: path/to/entry.ext
2. Calls: path/to/next.ext (via function/method name)
3. Delegates to: path/to/impl.ext
...

## Analysis
[Detailed architectural analysis including:
- Design patterns identified
- Component responsibilities
- Data flow description
- Interface contracts between components]

## Summary
[Concise 2-3 sentence summary answering the task question]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- File recall: Did you find the correct set of architecturally relevant files?
- Dependency accuracy: Did you trace the correct dependency/call chain?
- Architectural coherence: Did you correctly identify the design patterns and component relationships?

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the QuantLib barrier option pricing chain. Here's what I've delivered:

## Summary

I've traced the complete pricing chain for QuantLib barrier options and written a detailed architectural analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md`. The analysis covers:

### Key Findings:

1. **NPV() Entry Point** → Instrument.NPV() triggers LazyObject.calculate()

2. **Lazy Evaluation Framework**: The Instrument/LazyObject pattern defers expensive calculations until needed, caching results via a `calculated_` flag

3. **Pricing Engine Dispatch**: Via virtual methods, BarrierOption can use:
   - **AnalyticBarrierEngine**: Closed-form Haug formulas
   - **MCBarrierEngine**: Monte Carlo with Brownian bridge correction

4. **Monte Carlo Chain**:
   ```
   McSimulation → MonteCarloModel → PathGenerator → PathPricer
   ```
   - PathGenerator evolves GeneralizedBlackScholesProcess through a time grid
   - BarrierPathPricer checks barrier crossing and returns payoff or rebate

5. **Stochastic Process**: GeneralizedBlackScholesProcess queries term structures for:
   - **Rates**: YieldTermStructure.zeroRate() for drift (r, q)
   - **Volatility**: BlackVolTermStructure.blackVol(t, K) for diffusion σ

6. **Design Patterns**: Lazy Evaluation, Strategy (engines), Template Method (MC framework), Traits (path types), Handle-Body (term structures)

The analysis document includes detailed dependency chains, component responsibilities, data flow diagrams, interface contracts, and architectural patterns that demonstrate how each piece fits into the pricing system.

When the results depend\n84:                      on arguments which could change between\n85:                      invocations, the lazy object must register itself\n86:                      as observer of such objects for the calculations\n87:                      to be performed again when they change.\n88: \n89:             \\warning Should this method be redefined in derived\n90:                      classes, LazyObject::calculate() should be called\n91:                      in the overriding method.\n92:         */\n93:         virtual void calculate() const;\n94:         /*! This method must implement any calculations which must be\n95:             (re)done in order to calculate the desired results.\n96:         */\n97:         virtual void performCalculations() const = 0;\n98:         //@}\n99: \n100:       public:\n101:         //! \\name Notification settings\n102:         //@{\n103:         /*! The default can be\n112:             changed at compile time, or at at run time by calling\n113:             `LazyObject::Defaults::instance().alwaysForwardNotifications()`;\n114:             the run-time change won't affect lazy objects already created.\n115:         */\n116:         void forwardFirstNotificationOnly();\n117: \n118:         /*! Term Structure Hierarchy\n```\nYieldTermStructure [ql/termstructures/yieldtermstructure.hpp:46]\n  \u251c\u2500 discount(Time t) \u2192 compute discount factor\n  \u251c\u2500 zeroRate(Time t) \u2192 blackVariance(Time t, Real strike) \u2192 variance\n  \u2514\u2500 Implementations: BlackConstantVol, BlackVarianceCurve, ImpliedVolTermStructure, etc.\n```\n\n## Detailed Analysis\n\n### Design Patterns Identified\n\n#### 1. **Lazy Evaluation Pattern** (ql/patterns/lazyobject.hpp)\n- **Purpose**: Defer expensive calculations until results are actually requested\n- **Implementation**: LazyObject maintains `calculated_` flag and only runs `performCalculations()` once\n- **Benefit**: Results are cached; repeated queries don't recompute\n- **Observer Pattern Integration**: When observed objects change (rates, volatility), LazyObject.update() clears the flag to trigger recalculation\n\n#### 2. **Strategy Pattern** (Pricing Engines)\n- **Purpose**: Encapsulate different pricing algorithms (analytic vs. Monte Carlo)\n- **Interface**: BarrierOption::engine base class with pure virtual calculate()\n- **Implementations**: AnalyticBarrierEngine, MCBarrierEngine, FdBlackScholesBarrierEngine\n- **Dispatch**: Via Instrument.performCalculations() \u2192 engine_->calculate()\n\n#### 3. **Template Method Pattern** (McSimulation)\n- **Purpose**: Define skeleton of Monte Carlo algorithm, let subclasses define pathGenerator(), pathPricer(), timeGrid()\n- **Base**: McSimulation<MC, RNG, S> provides calculate(), value(), valueWithSamples()\n- **Subclass**: MCBarrierEngine implements pathGenerator(), pathPricer(), timeGrid()\n\n#### 4. **Traits Pattern** (mctraits.hpp)\n- **Purpose**: Parametrize path_generator_type and path_pricer_type by model dimensionality\n- **SingleVariate**: Path, PathPricer<Path>, PathGenerator<GSG>\n- **MultiVariate**: MultiPath, PathPricer<MultiPath>, MultiPathGenerator<GSG>\n\n#### 5. **Handle-Body Idiom** (Term Structures)\n- **Purpose**: Encapsulate reference-counted term structure objects\n- **Handle**: Handle<YieldTermStructure>, Handle<BlackVolTermStructure>\n- **Body**: Actual implementation (e.g., FlatForward, BlackConstantVol)\n- **Benefit**: Cheap copying via shared_ptr; automatic updates via observer pattern\n\n### Component Responsibilities\n\n| Component | Responsibility |\n|-----------|-----------------|\n| **BarrierOption** | Data container: barrier type, level, rebate, payoff, exercise date |\n| **Instrument** | Lazy evaluation orchestration: triggers calculate(), manages results caching |\n| **LazyObject** | Deferred computation: only runs performCalculations() if calculated_ == false |\n| **PricingEngine** | Algorithm encapsulation: computes price given instrument arguments |\n| **AnalyticBarrierEngine** | Closed-form pricing: applies Haug formulas directly |\n| **MCBarrierEngine** | Simulation-based pricing: creates paths and pricers via templates |\n| **McSimulation** | MC algorithm skeleton: samples paths until tolerance achieved |\n| **MonteCarloModel** | Sample accumulation: calls pathGenerator, pathPricer in loop |\n| **PathGenerator** | Path evolution: evolves process through time grid; applies Brownian bridge |\n| **GeneralizedBlackScholesProcess** | Dynamics specification: ln(S) drift = (r - q - \u03c3\u00b2/2), diffusion = \u03c3 |\n| **BarrierPathPricer** | Path payoff: checks barrier crossing, returns rebate or discounted payoff |\n| **YieldTermStructure** | Interest-rate surface: provides discount factors for all maturities |\n| **BlackVolTermStructure** | Volatility surface: provides Black volatility for all (T, K) pairs |\n\n### Data Flow in Monte Carlo Path Generation\n\n```\nTimeGrid (e.g., [0, 0.1, 0.2, ..., T])\n  \u2193\nGSG (Gaussian Sequence Generator) produces N independent N(0,1) random vars\n  \u2193\nBrownianBridge.transform() converts to path shocks (if brownianBridge=true)\n  \u2193\nPathGenerator evolves process:\n  For i = 1 to timeSteps:\n    drift = r(t[i-1]) - q(t[i-1]) - \u03c3(t[i-1], x[i-1])\u00b2/2\n      \u2193 queries YieldTermStructure.zeroRate() for r, q\n      \u2193 queries BlackVolTermStructure.blackVol() for \u03c3\n    diffusion = \u03c3(t[i-1], x[i-1])\n    x[i] = process.evolve(t[i-1], x[i-1], dt, \u03b5[i])\n      \u2193 applies Euler step: \u0394x = drift*dt + diffusion*\u221adt*\u03b5\n  \u2193\nBarrierPathPricer evaluates path:\n  For j = 0 to timeSteps:\n    If S[j] < barrier or S[j] > barrier (depending on type):\n      return rebate * discount(t[j])  \u2190 queries YieldTermStructure.discount()\n  If barrier never triggered:\n    return payoff(S[T]) * discount(T)\n  \u2193\nMonteCarloModel.sampleAccumulator_.add(price, weight)\n```\n\n### Interface Contracts\n\n#### GeneralizedBlackScholesProcess \u2194 PathGenerator\n```cpp\nprocess_->x0()                           // Initial stock price\nprocess_->drift(t, x)                    // Deterministic drift\nprocess_->diffusion(t, x)                // Volatility coefficient\nprocess_->evolve(t, x, dt, dw)           // Euler step with random shock\nprocess_->riskFreeRate()->discount(t)    // Discount factor\nprocess_->blackVolatility()->blackVol(t, strike)  // Black volatility\n```\n\n#### PathPricer \u2194 MonteCarloModel\n```cpp\npathPricer_(path)  // operator() returns Real (price for one path)\n```\n\n#### McSimulation \u2194 MCBarrierEngine\n```cpp\npathGenerator()    // virtual method returns ext::shared_ptr<path_generator_type>\npathPricer()       // virtual method returns ext::shared_ptr<path_pricer_type>\ntimeGrid()         // virtual method returns TimeGrid\ncalculate()        // template method provided by McSimulation\n```\n\n### Variance Reduction Techniques\n\nThe MCBarrierEngine supports:\n1. **Brownian Bridge Correction**: Reduces bias from discrete-time monitoring by interpolating barrier crossing probability between time steps\n2. **Antithetic Variates**: Each path is paired with its negated version, reducing variance\n3. **Biased Estimator Option**: Uses simpler payoff pricing for speed (isBiased_ flag)\n\n## Summary\n\nThe QuantLib barrier option pricing chain exemplifies a **modular, composable architecture** where:\n\n1. **NPV() call** triggers lazy evaluation through the Instrument-LazyObject framework\n2. **Pricing engine dispatch** (analytic vs. Monte Carlo) happens via virtual methods\n3. **Monte Carlo simulation** abstracts path generation and pricer through templates and traits\n4. **Path evolution** couples a stochastic process (GeneralizedBlackScholesProcess) with a sequence generator, querying term structures for parameters at each step\n5. **Term structure hierarchy** provides discount factors and volatilities as time-dependent surfaces, enabling market-consistent pricing\n\nThe architecture separates concerns: **instrument specification** (barriers, payoffs) from **pricing methodology** (closed-form vs. simulation), which is separated from **stochastic models** (Black-Scholes, Heston), which are separated from **calibrated market data** (term structures). This design enables swapping engines, processes, and market data independently, making QuantLib highly extensible.\n",

Interface Contracts\n\n#### GeneralizedBlackScholesProcess \u2194 PathGenerator\n```cpp\nprocess_->x0()                           // Initial stock price\nprocess_->drift(t, x)                    // Deterministic drift\nprocess_->diffusion(t, x)                // Volatility coefficient\nprocess_->evolve(t, x, dt, dw)           // Euler step with random shock\nprocess_->riskFreeRate()->discount(t)    // Discount factor\nprocess_->blackVolatility()->blackVol(t, strike)  // Black volatility\n```\n\n#### PathPricer \u2194 MonteCarloModel\n```cpp\npathPricer_(path)  // operator() returns Real (price for one path)\n```\n\n#### McSimulation \u2194 MCBarrierEngine\n```cpp\npathGenerator()    // virtual method returns ext::shared_ptr<path_generator_type>\npathPricer()       // virtual method returns ext::shared_ptr<path_pricer_type>\ntimeGrid()         // virtual method returns TimeGrid\ncalculate()        // template method provided by McSimulation\n```\n\n### Variance Reduction Techniques\n\nThe MCBarrierEngine supports:\n1. **Brownian Bridge Correction**: Reduces bias from discrete-time monitoring by interpolating barrier crossing probability between time steps\n2. **Antithetic Variates**: Each path is paired with its negated version, reducing variance\n3. **Biased Estimator Option**: Uses simpler payoff pricing for speed (isBiased_ flag)\n\n## Summary\n\nThe QuantLib barrier option pricing chain exemplifies a **modular, composable architecture** where:\n\n1. **NPV() call** triggers lazy evaluation through the Instrument-LazyObject framework\n2. **Pricing engine dispatch** (analytic vs. Monte Carlo) happens via virtual methods\n3. **Monte Carlo simulation** abstracts path generation and pricer through templates and traits\n4. **Path evolution** couples a stochastic process (GeneralizedBlackScholesProcess) with a sequence generator, querying term structures for parameters at each step\n5. **Term structure hierarchy** provides discount factors and volatilities as time-dependent surfaces, enabling market-consistent pricing\n\nThe architecture separates concerns: **instrument specification** (barriers, payoffs) from **pricing methodology** (closed-form vs. simulation), which is separated from **stochastic models** (Black-Scholes, Heston), which are separated from **calibrated market data** (term structures). This design enables swapping engines, processes, and market data independently, making QuantLib highly extensible.\n",

# QuantLib Barrier Option Pricing Chain Analysis

## Files Examined

### Core Instrument Files
- **ql/instruments/barrieroption.hpp** — Barrier option instrument definition with barrier type, level, and rebate parameters
- **ql/instruments/barrieroption.cpp** — BarrierOption implementation, constructor, and setupArguments() method
- **ql/instruments/oneassetoption.hpp** — Base class for single-asset options, defines greek calculation interface
- **ql/instruments/oneassetoption.cpp** — Calls calculate() to trigger lazy evaluation chain

### Lazy Evaluation Framework
- **ql/instrument.hpp** — Abstract instrument base class extending LazyObject; defines NPV(), calculate(), and performCalculations()
- **ql/patterns/lazyobject.hpp** — Framework for lazy evaluation with caching; manages calculated_ flag and deferred computation

### Pricing Engines
- **ql/pricingengines/barrier/analyticbarrierengine.hpp** — Closed-form barrier option pricing using analytical formulas (Haug)
- **ql/pricingengines/barrier/mcbarrierengine.hpp** — Monte Carlo barrier engine with Brownian bridge correction; defines BarrierPathPricer and BiasedBarrierPathPricer
- **ql/pricingengines/mcsimulation.hpp** — Base class for Monte Carlo engines; template provides framework for sampling and tolerance control

### Monte Carlo Framework
- **ql/methods/montecarlo/montecarlomodel.hpp** — Generic Monte Carlo model: connects PathGenerator, PathPricer, and Statistics accumulator
- **ql/methods/montecarlo/pathgenerator.hpp** — Generates paths by evolving stochastic process through time grid using random numbers
- **ql/methods/montecarlo/mctraits.hpp** — Type traits defining path_generator_type and path_pricer_type for single/multi-variate models

### Stochastic Processes
- **ql/processes/blackscholesprocess.hpp**
